<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">2019 video game</div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1316064257">.mw-parser-output class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Google_Stadia" title="Google Stadia">Stadia</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Release</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409" /><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><b>PS4</b>, <b>Windows</b>, <b>Xbox One</b></li><li>22 March 2019</li><li><b>Stadia</b></li><li>28 October 2020</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Video_game_genre" title="Video game genre">Genre</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Action-adventure" class="mw-redirect" title="Action-adventure">Action-adventure</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Mode</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Single-player" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-player">Single-player</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><i><b>Sekiro: Shadows Die Twice</b></i><sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Action-adventure_game" title="Action-adventure game">action-adventure game</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/FromSoftware" title="FromSoftware">FromSoftware</a>. It was released in Japan by FromSoftware and internationally by <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>  for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a> in March 2019 and for <a href="/wiki/Google_Stadia" title="Google Stadia">Stadia</a> in October 2020. 
</p><p>Players control Wolf, a <a href="/wiki/Shinobi" class="mw-redirect" title="Shinobi">shinobi</a> who embarks on a quest to rescue his lord, and becomes embroiled into a conflict for Ashina's fate. The gameplay is focused on stealth, exploration, and combat, with a particular emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Boss_(video_gaming)" class="mw-redirect" title="Boss (video gaming)">boss battles</a>. It takes place in a fictionalized Japan during the <a href="/wiki/Sengoku_period" title="Sengoku period">Sengoku period</a> and makes strong references to <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_mythology" title="Buddhist mythology">Buddhist mythology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_philosophy" title="Buddhist philosophy">philosophy</a>. Lead director <a href="/wiki/Hidetaka_Miyazaki" title="Hidetaka Miyazaki">Hidetaka Miyazaki</a> wanted to create a new <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_property" title="Intellectual property">intellectual property</a> (IP) that marked a departure from their <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Souls" title="Dark Souls">Dark Souls</a></i> series, wanting to make a Japanese-themed game around shinobi and ninja. <i><a href="/wiki/Tenchu" title="Tenchu">Tenchu</a></i>, as an IP tied to FromSoftware and with that history theme, ended up being the impetus for the project.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p><i>Sekiro</i> received acclaim from critics, who praised its gameplay and setting and compared it favorably to FromSoftware's past work, although opinions on its heavy difficulty were mixed. It won several year-end awards, including <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Award_for_Game_of_the_Year" title="The Game Award for Game of the Year">the Game Award for Game of the Year</a>, and has sold over ten million units as of September 2023.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Gameplay">Gameplay</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sekiro:_Shadows_Die_Twice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Gameplay"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Sekiro_-_Shadows_Die_Twice_pre-release_gameplay_screenshot.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a8/Sekiro_-_Shadows_Die_Twice_pre-release_gameplay_screenshot.png/250px-Sekiro_-_Shadows_Die_Twice_pre-release_gameplay_screenshot.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a8/Sekiro_-_Shadows_Die_Twice_pre-release_gameplay_screenshot.png 2x" data-file-width="421" data-file-height="237" /></a><figcaption>Screenshot showing the player fighting against one of the game's many bosses, the True Monk</figcaption></figure>
<p><i>Sekiro: Shadows Die Twice</i> is an <a href="/wiki/Action-adventure_game" title="Action-adventure game">action-adventure game</a> played from a <a href="/wiki/Third-person_view" class="mw-redirect" title="Third-person view">third-person view</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-polygon&#95;e3&#95;2018&#95;3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polygon_e3_2018-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-GameplayPreview&#95;5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameplayPreview-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Engadget&#95;6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engadget-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Compared to <a href="/wiki/FromSoftware" title="FromSoftware">FromSoftware</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Souls" title="Dark Souls">Dark Souls</a></i> series, the game features fewer <a href="/wiki/Role-playing_video_game" title="Role-playing video game">role-playing</a> elements, lacks <a href="/wiki/Character_creation" title="Character creation">character creation</a> and the ability to level up a variety of stats, and has no <a href="/wiki/Real-time_communication" title="Real-time communication">real-time</a> <a href="/wiki/Multiplayer" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiplayer">multiplayer</a> elements.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GameplayPreview&#95;5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameplayPreview-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Engadget&#95;6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engadget-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Variety&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It does, however, include gear upgrading, special abilities with a prosthetic arm, a skill tree, and limited ability customization. Rather than attacking to whittle an enemy's <a href="/wiki/Health_points" class="mw-redirect" title="Health points">health points</a>, combat in <i>Sekiro</i> revolves around using a <a href="/wiki/Katana" title="Katana">katana</a> to attack their posture and balance instead, as well as deflecting incoming enemy attacks, eventually leading to an opening that allows for a single killing blow.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GameplayPreview&#95;5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameplayPreview-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The game also features <a href="/wiki/Stealth_game" title="Stealth game">stealth</a> elements, allowing players to instantly eliminate or severely damage most enemies if they can get in range undetected.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GameplayPreview&#95;5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameplayPreview-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In addition, the player character can use various tools to assist with combat and exploration, such as a <a href="/wiki/Grappling_hook" title="Grappling hook">grappling hook</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GameplayPreview&#95;5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameplayPreview-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> If the player character <a href="/wiki/Life_(gaming)" class="mw-redirect" title="Life (gaming)">dies</a>, they can be revived on the spot if they have resurrection power, which is restored by defeating enemies, instead of <a href="/wiki/Respawning" class="mw-redirect" title="Respawning">respawning</a> at earlier checkpoints.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GameplayPreview&#95;5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameplayPreview-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Synopsis">Synopsis</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sekiro:_Shadows_Die_Twice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Synopsis"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>During the late <a href="/wiki/Sengoku_period" title="Sengoku period">Sengoku period</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ashina_clan_(Japan)" title="Ashina clan (Japan)">Ashina clan</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Kensei_(honorary_title)" title="Kensei (honorary title)">Kensei</a> Isshin Ashina, seizes a land rich in divine favor, including a foreign deity dubbed the Divine Dragon which can grant immortality through a bloodline dubbed the "Dragon's Heritage" and through the Rejuvenating Waters and its <a href="/wiki/Scolopendra_subspinipes" title="Scolopendra subspinipes">mukade</a>-infested Sediment. During this time, a nameless orphan is adopted by the wandering <a href="/wiki/Shinobi" class="mw-redirect" title="Shinobi">shinobi</a> Owl, who names the boy "Wolf" and trains him in his ways. As Wolf grows up, Owl entrusts him with safeguarding the young lord Kuro, the last of the Dragon's Heritage line.
</p><p>Two decades later, the now-elderly Isshin is on his deathbed and the weakened Ashina is besieged by the forces of the <a href="/wiki/Naidaijin" title="Naidaijin">Interior Ministry</a> to finish the <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">unification of Japan</a>. Desperate to save his clan, Isshin's adoptive grandson, Genichiro, seeks Kuro to use his blood to create an immortal army. Disagreeing with his grandson's methods, Isshin has his private physician, Emma, warn Wolf so the two can flee. However, Genichiro confronts them and defeats Wolf in a duel, severing his left arm and capturing Kuro. Wolf is saved by a man called the Sculptor, who gifts him a <a href="/wiki/Prosthesis" title="Prosthesis">prosthetic</a> arm. To rescue Kuro, Wolf assaults Ashina Castle, where he meets Isshin and is given a new name: "Sekiro". Optionally, Sekiro can revisit his past through meditation using various items he finds; three years ago, Kuro's home was raided by bandits led by the shinobi Lady Butterfly, leading to Owl's apparent death. While Sekiro defeated her, he was fatally stabbed by an unknown assailant and only survived after Kuro shared his blood with him.
</p><p>Sekiro again duels Genichiro and defeats him this time. However, he survives, having used the Sediment from the Rejuvenating Waters to gain corrupted immortality, and escapes. Afterward, Kuro refuses to flee and instead wants Sekiro to perform the Immortal Severance ritual on him, which would result in his death and eliminate the Dragon's Heritage. Sekiro reluctantly agrees and sets out to collect the necessary materials for the ritual, including a weapon that can kill immortals known as the Mortal Blade from the Divine Child – the sole survivor of experiments with the Rejuvenating Waters. After collecting most of the ritual elements, Sekiro is confronted by Owl, who faked his death in pursuit of the Dragon's Heritage and revealed to be the one who stabbed him three years ago. If Sekiro renounces his loyalty to Kuro on Owl's orders, he fights and kills Emma and Isshin while Owl kills Genichiro. However, Sekiro then becomes corrupted by bloodlust and kills Owl as well while Kuro watches in horror, leading to the <i><a href="/wiki/Asura_(Buddhism)" title="Asura (Buddhism)">Shura</a></i> ending. 
</p><p>If Sekiro refuses, he kills Owl in combat and enters the divine realm to recover the final ingredient for the ritual from the Divine Dragon itself. Upon returning to the mortal realm, Sekiro discovers that Isshin has passed and Ashina is under attack by the Interior Ministry's troops who have set fire to the castle with <a href="/wiki/B%C5%8D-hiya" title="Bō-hiya">rockets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tezutsu-hanabi" title="Tezutsu-hanabi">flamethrowers</a>. Fighting through the burning castle, Sekiro eventually finds Kuro under attack by Genichiro, who has retrieved another Mortal Blade. Upon defeat, Genichiro sacrifices himself using the second Mortal Blade to revive Isshin in his prime so he might restore Ashina, a wish that his grandfather attempts to honor despite disagreeing with it. After killing Isshin, depending on the items gathered, three endings are available:
</p>
<ul><li>In the <i>Immortal Severance</i> ending, Sekiro performs the ritual as instructed, killing Kuro and making himself mortal again. Afterward, like the Sculptor before him, Sekiro spends his remaining days carving Buddha statues while keeping his prosthetic to pass on to someone else one day.</li>
<li>In the <i>Purification</i> ending, Sekiro performs an alternate ritual worked out with Emma's aid which has Sekiro sacrificing himself while freeing Kuro of the Dragon's Heritage. Afterward, Kuro prays at Sekiro's grave with Emma before departing Ashina.</li>
<li>In the <i>Return</i> ending, Sekiro collaborates with the Divine Child to make her a vessel for the Divine Dragon's power. After defeating Isshin, Sekiro takes the dying Kuro to the Divine Child, who absorbs him into herself. The Divine Child and Sekiro then leave on a journey to return the Dragon's Heritage to its home in the West.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Development">Development</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sekiro:_Shadows_Die_Twice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Hidetaka_Miyazaki,_The_Game_Awards_2022_(cropped).png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hidetaka_Miyazaki%2C_The_Game_Awards_2022_%28cropped%29.png/250px-Hidetaka_Miyazaki%2C_The_Game_Awards_2022_%28cropped%29.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="300" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hidetaka_Miyazaki%2C_The_Game_Awards_2022_%28cropped%29.png/500px-Hidetaka_Miyazaki%2C_The_Game_Awards_2022_%28cropped%29.png 2x" data-file-width="725" data-file-height="1089" /></a><figcaption><i>Sekiro</i> was directed by <a href="/wiki/Hidetaka_Miyazaki" title="Hidetaka Miyazaki">Hidetaka Miyazaki</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Development of <i>Sekiro</i> began in late 2015 following the completion of <i><a href="/wiki/Bloodborne" title="Bloodborne">Bloodborne</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a>, <i>The Old Hunters</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-WeeklyFamitsu&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WeeklyFamitsu-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was directed by <a href="/wiki/Hidetaka_Miyazaki" title="Hidetaka Miyazaki">Hidetaka Miyazaki</a>, who had previously worked on the <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Souls" title="Dark Souls">Dark Souls</a></i> series and <i><a href="/wiki/Bloodborne" title="Bloodborne">Bloodborne</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-gameinformer&#95;director&#95;11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gameinformer_director-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Sekiro</i> draws inspiration from the <i><a href="/wiki/Tenchu" title="Tenchu">Tenchu</a></i> series of stealth-action games developed by <a href="/wiki/Acquire_(company)" title="Acquire (company)">Acquire</a> and published by FromSoftware.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The team initially considered developing the game as a sequel to <i>Tenchu;</i> however, it quickly outgrew the concept.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Miyazaki intended the combat changes to capture the feel of "swords clashing", with fighters trying to create an opening to deliver the fatal strike.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GameplayPreview&#95;5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameplayPreview-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He and the team also created the game to be an entirely <a href="/wiki/Single-player" class="mw-redirect" title="Single-player">single-player</a> experience, as they believed <a href="/wiki/Multiplayer" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiplayer">multiplayer</a> to have limitations they wanted to avoid.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Variety&#95;8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Variety-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite the game taking place during the <a href="/wiki/Sengoku" class="mw-redirect" title="Sengoku">Sengoku</a> period of real-world Japanese history, no historical people or locations are featured in the game.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-storytelling&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-storytelling-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The game was revealed via a <a href="/wiki/Teaser_trailer" title="Teaser trailer">teaser trailer</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards_2017" title="The Game Awards 2017">the Game Awards 2017</a> in December, showing the tagline "Shadows Die Twice".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-gameinformer&#95;teaser&#95;15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gameinformer_teaser-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The game's full title was revealed to be <i>Sekiro: Shadows Die Twice</i> during <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s press conference at <a href="/wiki/E3_2018" title="E3 2018">E3 2018</a>. The game was published by <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a> worldwide, with FromSoftware self-publishing it in Japan and Cube Game publishing in the Asia-Pacific region.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Sekiro</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> soundtrack was composed by Yuka Kitamura,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with some contributions from <a href="/wiki/Noriyuki_Asakura" title="Noriyuki Asakura">Noriyuki Asakura</a>. The game was released for <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_4" title="PlayStation 4">PlayStation 4</a>, <a href="/wiki/Windows" class="mw-redirect" title="Windows">Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_One" title="Xbox One">Xbox One</a> on 22 March 2019.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-release&#95;19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-release-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A collectors edition was also released the same day and included a steelbook case, a figurine of the protagonist, an art book, a physical map of the game's world, a download code for the soundtrack, and in-game coin replicas.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-release&#95;19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-release-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A port for <a href="/wiki/Google_Stadia" title="Google Stadia">Stadia</a> was released in late 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 31 October 2020, a free update was released that added new content to the game, such as new cosmetics for Wolf and a boss rush game mode.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The word "sekirō" (隻狼) is a contraction of "sekiwan no ōkami" (隻腕の狼), which translates as "one-armed wolf."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Title&#95;Meaning&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Title_Meaning-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The subtitle "Shadows Die Twice" was initially meant to be used as a slogan for the teaser trailer until Activision requested it be kept for the final name.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-GameplayPreview&#95;5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameplayPreview-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p><i>Sekiro</i> received critical acclaim.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> website <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, it garnered "universal acclaim" for the PlayStation 4 and Xbox One versions and "generally favorable reviews" for the Windows version.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-MCPC&#95;24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPC-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-MCPS4&#95;25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCPS4-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-MCXONE&#95;26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCXONE-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/OpenCritic" title="OpenCritic">OpenCritic</a> determined that 96% of critics recommend the game.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-OC&#95;27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OC-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many critics praised the game's combat for departing from the typical style of FromSoftware's other similar games. In a review for <i><a href="/wiki/Destructoid" title="Destructoid">Destructoid</a></i>, Chris Carter described open combat as "akin to a waltz" and praised the variety of ways the combat could be approached, writing that players had more choices than in <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Souls" title="Dark Souls">Dark Souls</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Bloodborne" title="Bloodborne">Bloodborne</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Brandin Tyrell from <i><a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a></i> praised the game's focus on "split-second swordsmanship", and although "to any Souls veteran, <i>Sekiro</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> timing-based lock-on combat of strikes and slashes is familiar", the game's "sense of safety" caused the combat to feel "refreshing and new".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto2&#95;35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/PC_Gamer" title="PC Gamer">PC Gamer</a></i> journalist Tom Senior called the combat "beautiful" and praised the posture system, writing that "instead of chipping down health bars until the enemy keels over, you overwhelm their posture bar with strikes and perfect parries until an opening appears, and then finish with a deathblow".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He stated that the system takes "the catharsis" of beating a great boss and "focuses all that emotion into one split second". In a review for the website <i><a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a></i>, Tamoor Hussain wrote that the game "rewrites the rules of engagement", stating that, while previous FromSoftware games demanded quick decision-making, <i>Sekiro</i> "pushes these demands further" than ever before. Reviewers also praised the resurrection mechanic, with Carter calling it "genius", and the stealth options, which gave the player freedom without descending into frustration.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto&#95;28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The level design was also praised. Particular emphasis was given to the player's increased verticality due to the addition of the grappling hook and a dedicated jump button. Tyrell wrote that the grappling hook "sends ripples throughout the gameplay", writing that "where all previous Soulsborne characters felt rooted firmly to the ground as they trudged down hallways and slowly climbed ladders, <i>Sekiro</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> <a href="/wiki/Level_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Level design">level design</a> has permission to be much more vertical". Carter wrote that the hook provided "a more vertical and in some cases more challenging level design from an exploration standpoint". Senior wrote that the game used "large but separate zones rather than a huge connected world" but praised the "many secrets hidden just off the critical path, often reached with the excellent grappling hook, which lets you vault between tree branches and rooftops". The levels themselves were also praised, with Hussain writing that "buildings are placed together to encourage exploration and reconnaissance, with roofs almost touching so that you can leap between them and scope out all angles", with the branching paths "creating that satisfying feeling of venturing into the unknown and then emerging into the familiar".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-auto1&#95;33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Reaction to the lack of online multiplayer was mixed. Several reviewers noted that this allowed the game to have a full pause button, which was praised. However, Tyrell noted that he "missed the small notes left by others in the world alerting me to imminent threats or hidden secrets, or that vague sense that danger lurks behind me in the form of an invading player" that defined the experience of playing "Soulsborne" games. He also noticed the "lack of PvP battles, which seem[ed] like a waste of the new emphasis on skill-based swordsmanship" and argued that the deflecting and blocking mechanics would have suited online play.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Tyrrel&#95;Review&#95;45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tyrrel_Review-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly to other FromSoftware games, the game's high difficulty level polarised players and journalists. Several reviewers praised the difficulty, with Senior calling it "brutal" but "spectacular". Hussain wrote that the game "punishes you for missteps" and was "suited for people of a certain temperament and with a very specific, slightly masochistic taste in games" but argued that victory was "intense" and "gratifying". Tyrell wrote that the combat had a "steep curve to mastering it" but argued it was "somewhat easier than its predecessors" while still providing the sense of being "the greatest swordsman that ever lived" after tough victories. However, several journalists found it too challenging, with Don Rowe from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spinoff" title="The Spinoff">The Spinoff</a></i> calling it "infuriating" and writing that he was not having fun after six hours with the game.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Several days after the game was released, modders managed to develop <a href="/wiki/Mod_(video_gaming)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mod (video gaming)">mods</a> which would make the game easier by changing the speed of the player's character relative to the game.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> James Davenport of <i>PC Gamer</i> said that the game's final boss was too difficult for him to beat without the help of the software.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sales">Sales</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sekiro:_Shadows_Die_Twice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sales"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On release day, <i>Sekiro</i> drew over 108,000 concurrent players on <a href="/wiki/Steam_(service)" title="Steam (service)">Steam</a>, the highest for a new game launched during January–March 2019 and the third highest of any Japanese game in the platform's history, behind only <i><a href="/wiki/Monster_Hunter:_World" title="Monster Hunter: World">Monster Hunter: World</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Souls_III" title="Dark Souls III">Dark Souls III</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-eurogamer&#95;49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogamer-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later in March, it had reached over 125,000 concurrent players on Steam, making it one of the most played games on the platform at the time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  
</p><p>In its debut week, <i>Sekiro</i> topped the UK and <a href="/wiki/EMEAA" class="mw-redirect" title="EMEAA">EMEAA</a> (Europe, Middle East, Africa, Asia) charts, surpassing <i><a href="/wiki/Tom_Clancy%27s_The_Division_2" title="Tom Clancy&#39;s The Division 2">Tom Clancy's The Division 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In Japan, the game debuted first, with 157,548 retail units sold in its opening weekend.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>  
</p><p>Within ten days of its release, over two<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million units were sold, which rose to over five million by July 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of September 2023, it has sold over 10 million units.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>   
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Awards">Awards</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sekiro:_Shadows_Die_Twice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Awards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The game won several awards, including <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Award_for_Game_of_the_Year" title="The Game Award for Game of the Year">Game of the Year</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards_2019" title="The Game Awards 2019">the Game Awards 2019</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-TGA2019&#95;59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TGA2019-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> by editors of <i><a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a></i>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and by fans in the <a href="/wiki/2019_Steam_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 Steam Awards">2019 Steam Awards</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Anime_adaptation">Anime adaptation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sekiro:_Shadows_Die_Twice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Anime adaptation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> adaptation, titled <i>Sekiro: No Defeat</i>, was announced at <a href="/wiki/Gamescom" title="Gamescom">Gamescom</a> 2025. The series is produced by Qzil.la and is set to premiere in 2026, with <a href="/wiki/Crunchyroll" title="Crunchyroll">Crunchyroll</a> streaming the series outside of Japan. The three main cast of the game, <a href="/wiki/Daisuke_Namikawa" title="Daisuke Namikawa">Daisuke Namikawa</a> (Wolf), Miyuki Satou (Kuro), and <a href="/wiki/Kenjiro_Tsuda" title="Kenjiro Tsuda">Kenjiro Tsuda</a> (Genichiro Ashina), reprise their roles.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A theatrical edition of the anime is set to open in Japanese theaters in the same year.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
